Jamison Brereton

66 (582)
Mitra and Varun╠гa (1тАУ3, 17тАУ19), A╠Дdityas (4тАУ13), Su╠Дrya (14тАУ16)
Vasiс╣гс╣нha Maitr─Бvaruс╣Зi
19 verses: g─Бyatr─л 1тАУ9, 17тАУ19, arranged in trcas; br ╠е hat ╠е ─л alternating with satobr╠еhat─л 10тАУ15, arranged in prag─Бthas; purau╠Ис╣гс╣Зih 16
This hymn consists of eight metrical units of various meters. The first three are three g─Бyatr─л tr╠еcas, followed by three br╠еhat─л/satobr╠еhat─л strophes and one more g─Бyatr─л tr╠еca. The hymn then concludes with a final, single purau╠Ис╣гс╣Зih verse. Despite its metrical complexity, the hymn sustains its basic themes throughout. Once again this is a hymn recited at sunrise, and indeed the phrase тАЬat the rising of the sunтАЭ occurs at the beginning of three of its seven strophes (vss. 4, 7, 12). Also the beginning of fourth strophe (vs. 14) contains a variant of the phrase, the final tr╠еca starts (vs. 16) with a reference to the rising of the sun, and the prag─Бtha beginning at verse 10 opens with a mention of the sun. Therefore of the hymnтАЩs eight units, only the first tr╠еca (vss. 1тАУ3), which establishes Mitra and Varuс╣Зa as the dedicands of the hymn, and the final summary invitation to Mitra and Varuс╣Зa lack a reference to the rising sun in its first verse. This repeated mention of the rising sun is a structuring device that unifies the hymn despite the diversity of its meter. Thematically, the rise and movement of the Sun across the heavens becomes the representation of the ─АdityasтАЩ lordship extending across the world.
The actions of the ─Аdityas are also linked with the words and action of the ritual. This theme is introduced at the outset, when they are described as suda╠Бkс╣гa тАЬof good skillтАЭ and the children of Dakс╣гa, the embodiment of skill and specifically sacrificial skill (vs. 2). The gods sustain тАЬthe three divisionsтАЭ (vs. 10), a phrase that likely refers both to the divisions of the world (earth, midspace, and heaven), and to the divisions of the ritual (the three soma-pressings). They also sustain the divi sions of time (vs. 11): the year, month, and day, but also the sacrifice and the night, a division that could refer to the sacrificial rites by day and the continuation of the rites across the night. The ─Аdityas тАЬimpelтАЭ (тИЪs┼л)тАФa word connected with Savitar, of course, and therefore with the ─АdityasтАФthe sacrificers and thereby bring their rituals success and take their worshipers тАЬacross difficult straitsтАЭ (vss. 4тАУ5).964 VII.66

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay Mitra, the destroyer of sin, Aryaman, Savit─Б, Bhaga, bestow (upon us), today at sun-rise what (wepray for).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

If today, at the rising of the sun, the one free of offense [=the Sun], Mitra, Aryaman,
Savitar, and Bhaga will each impel (us),

Griffith

So when the Sun hath risen to-day, may sinless Mitra, Aryaman,
Bhaga, and Savitar sendus forth.

Geldner

Wenn heute bei Sonnenaufgang Mitra, Aryaman, Savitri, Bhaga die Schuldlosen bestimmen werden,

Grassmann

Was bei der Sonne Aufgang heut der heil’ge Mitra, Arjaman, Bhaga und Savitar verleihn,

English translation:

тАЬMay this our dwelling be well protected, liberal deities, on your departure, you who purify us from sin.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Let this dwelling be one that ritually pursues (the gods) well. Now, o you bringing good drops, (let those go) forth on their course
who take us across difficult straits.

Griffith

May this our home be guarded well forward, ye Bounteous, on the way,
Who bear us safely o’er distress.

English translation:

тАЬAnd who are sovereign over all, and, with Aditi, preside over this unobstructed and great ceremony.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Utasvar─Бjo aditiradabdhasya vratasya ye maho r─Бj─Бna i┼Ыate: aditis teс╣г─Бm m─Бt─Б, of them Aditi is the mother,or mitr─Бdayo aditi┼Ыca = Mitra and the rest and Aditi

Jamison Brereton

And the sovereign kings and Aditi, who (are masters) of the undeceivable command,
as kings are masters of (all that is) great.

The Kings who rule a vast domain.

At the rising of the sun I will sing to you two, to Mitra and Varuс╣Зa, to Aryaman, who cares for the stranger.

Soon as the Sun hath risen, to you, to Mitra-Varuna, I sing,
And Aryaman who slays the foe.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay this praise (be effective) for unimpeached strength, alone with golden treasure; may it (beeffective), sages, for the fulfilment of (the objects of) the sacrifice.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

With longing for wealth and gold, this thought is for power that knows no wolf;
this inspired (thought) is for winning wisdom.

Griffith

With wealth of gold may this my song bring unmolested power and might,
And, Brahmans, gain the sacrifice.

Geldner

Aus Verlangen nach Reichtum, nach Gold gedichtet, soll dies Lied zur St├дrke, die vor R├дubern sichert, dies beredte Lied zum Gewinn des Opfers verhelfen.

Grassmann

Durch goldnen Reichthum sei dies Lied ein Quell der unversehrten Kraft Und, weise ihr, der Geistesmacht.

Elizarenkova

тАЬMay we be thine, divine Varuс╣Зa; may we, along with pious worshippers, be, Mitra, thine; may we obtainfood and water.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Iс╣гam svas ca dh─лmahi = annam udakam ca dh─Бray─Бmahe, may we retain food and water;the tс╣Ыca, i.e. this and the two preceding с╣Ыca’s are repeated at the morning sacrifice

Together with our patrons, might we be these, o god Varuс╣Зa, o Mitra: might we receive refreshment and the sun.

Food and Heaven’s light will we obtain.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬManifold radiant as the sun, Agni-tongued augmenters of sacrifice, you who have limited the threeuniversal sacrifices with comprehensive rites.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Limited: tr─лс╣Зi ye yemuс╕е vidath─Бni dh─лtibhiс╕е vi┼Ыv─Бniparibh┼лtibhiс╕е = ye tr─лс╣Зi vy─Бpt─Бni kс╣гity─Бdisth─Бn─Бni paribh─Бvukaiс╕е karmaiс╕е prayacchanti, who give thethree spread plural ces, earth and the rest, with overcoming acts; Mitra and the rest are worshipped as the objectsof three rites, with definite ceremonies or at definite seasons

Jamison Brereton

Many are they whose eye is the Sun, whose tongue is Agni, who strengthen through the truth,
who sustain the three divisions by their insights, all (the divisions) by their encompassing powers.

Griffith

Many are they who strengthen Law, Sun-eyed, with Agni for their tongue,
They who direct the three great gatherings with their thoughts, yea, all things with surpassing might.

charioteers of truth!

Even as Varuna, Mitra, Aryaman deserve: ye are the charioteers of Law.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAccepters of rites, genitive rated for rites, augmenters of rites, fierce enemies of the neglecter of rites, maywe, as well as those men who are your adorers, be in (the enjoyment of) the highest felicity, all confirmed by you.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Those men who are: teс╣г─Бm vaс╕е sumne succharidiс╣гс╣нame = of those of you in the most blissful opulence, or inhappiness, united with a most delightful dwelling, sukhatame dhane atyantaramaс╣З─лya gс╣Ыhayukte sukhe v─Б

Jamison Brereton

(You) possessing the truth, born of the truth, and strengthening through the truth, (you) terrifying haters of untruthтАФ
might we be in the most protective favor of you, o men, and might also our patrons.

Griffith

True to Law, born in Law the strengtheners of Law, terrible, haters of the false,
In their felicity which gives the best defence may we men and our princes dwell.

Geldner

Die Wahrhaftigen, aus der Wahrheit Geborenen, die Wahrheit Mehrenden, gef├╝rchteten, die Unwahrheit Hassenden-in deren sch├╝tzendster Gunst von euch, ihr Herren, m├╢chten wir sein und die Lohngeber.

Grassmann

Gerechte ihr, im Recht geboren und erstarkt, erhabne, Unrecht fassende, In eurem Schirm, o M├дnner, der am besten sch├╝tzt, lasst uns sein und die F├╝rstenschar.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe seven gliding steeds convey the sun, the lord of every individual moving or stationary thing,traversing the whole world in his chariot for the good (of all).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The lord: ┼Ы─лrс╣гс╣Зaс╕е ┼Ы─лrс╣гс╣Зo jagatastasthuс╣гaspatim. the lord of stationary and moveable head by head; ┼Ыiras is connected with the horses of thesun: ┼Ыirasa svasva┼Ыira sa vahanti s┼лryam, they bear the sun by his own head;

Head = a being with a head,┼Ыiraс╕е ┼Ыabdena tad van pad─Бrthaс╕е, that is to say, the whole of such objects, tasya kartsnyam, or the best of all,sarvasya ┼Ыreс╣гс╣нham; it thus implies only each or individual

Jamison Brereton

For his easy passage, the seven sistersтАФthe antelopes on his chariotтАФ convey the SunтАФ
the lord of each one, head by head, and of the moving and the
standingтАФthrough the whole dusky realm altogether.

Griffith

Lord of each single head, of fixt and moving things, equally through the whole expanse,
The Seven sister Bays bear Surya on his car, to bring us wealth and happiness.

Geldner

Den Herrn alles Lebenden-Haupt zum Haupt-und des Unbeweglichen, den Surya ziehen mitten durch den ganzen Luftkreis die sieben Schwestern, die Falbinnen am Wagen zu guter Fahrt.

Grassmann

Den Herrn jedweden Wesens, was da geht und steht, ihn ziehn im Nu durch allen Raum, Den Sonnengott die sieben Stuten, Schwestern sie, im Wagen hin zu hohem Glanz.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬThat pure eye (of the universe), beneficial of the gods, rises; may we behold it for a hundred years; maywe live a hundred years.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Yajus. 36.24 adds: ┼Ыс╣Ыс╣Зuy─Бma ┼Ыaradaс╕е ┼Ыatam, prabrav─Бma ┼Ыaradaс╕е ┼Ыatam,ad─лnaс╕е sy─Бma ┼Ыaradaс╕е ┼Ыatam, bh┼лy─Б┼Ыca ┼Ыaradaс╕е ┼Ыatam, may we hear, may we speak, may we beindependent, for a hundred years or more

Jamison Brereton

That eye, fixed in place by the gods, blazing as it ascends,
might we see for a hundred autumns. Might we live for a hundred
autumns!

Griffith

A hundred autumns may we see that bright Eye, God-ordained, arise
A hundred autumns may we live.

Geldner

Grassmann

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рдЖрдЬреНрдЮрд╛ рджреЗрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ рдХрд┐рд╣реЗ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╛рджрд┐ рдпрдЬреНрдЮреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдЕрдиреБрд╖реНрдард╛рдиреА рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреЛрдВ ! рддреБрдо рд▓реЛрдЧ рд╕рддреНрдХрд╛рд░рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдХ рдЕрдкрдиреЗ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдиреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрдУ рдФрд░ рд╕реЛрдордкрд╛рди рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реБрдП рдЙрдирдХреЗ рд╣реГрджрдп рдХреЛ рд╢рд╛рдиреНрддрд┐рдзрд╛рдо рдмрдирд╛рдУ рдЕрд░реНрдерд╛рддреН рдЕрдкрдиреЗ рдЕрдиреБрд╖реНрдард╛рдирд░реВрдк рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди рд╕реЗ рдЙрдирдХреЛ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдпрдЬреНрдЮ, рдпреЛрдЧрдпрдЬреНрдЮ, рддрдерд╛ рдХрд░реНрдордпрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рджрд┐ рд╡реИрджрд┐рдХ рдХрд░реНрдореЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рдЕрдиреБрд╖реНрдард╛рдиреА рдмрдирд╛рдХрд░ рдкрд╡рд┐рддреНрд░ рдХрд░реЛ рдФрд░ рд╢рд╛рдиреНрддрд┐ рдХреА рдЖрд╣реБрддрд┐ рджреЗрддреЗ рд╣реБрдП рд╕рдВрд╕рд╛рд░ рднрд░ рдореЗрдВ рд╢рд╛рдиреНрддрд┐ рдлреИрд▓рд╛рдУ, рдЬреЛ рддреБрдореНрд╣рд╛рд░рд╛ рдХрд░реНрддреНрддрд╡реНрдп рд╣реИ реерезрепреерезрезрее рдпрд╣ ремрем рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдФрд░ резрез рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╡рд░реНрдЧ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдЖ рее

рдЖрд░реНрдпрдореБрдирд┐ - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЛрддрд╛рд╡реГрдзрд╛) рд╣реЗ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдпрдЬреНрдЮрдпреЛрдЧрдпрдЬреНрдЮрдХрд░реНрдордпрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рджрд┐рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╡рд░реНрджреНрдзрдпрд┐рддрд╛рд░реЛ рдорд┐рддреНрд░рд╛рд╡рд░реБрдгреМ, (рдирд░рд╛) рдирд░реМ ! рдпреБрд╡рд╛рдореН (рдЖ, рдпрд╛рддрдВ) рдЖрдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддрдВ (рдЖрд╣реБрддрд┐рдореН) рдордо рд╕рддреНрдХрд╛рд░рдореН (рдЬреБрд╖рд╛рдгреМ) рдЕрднрд┐рд▓рд╖реНрдпрдиреНрддреМ (рд╕реЛрдордореН, рдкрд╛рддрдВ) рд╕реЛрдордВ рдкрд┐рдмрддрдорд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ, рдЕрддреНрд░рд╛рдкрд┐ рджреНрд╡рд┐рд╡рдЪрдирдВ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╢рдХреНрддрд┐рджреНрд╡рдпрд╕реВрдЪрдирд╛рд░реНрдердореН реерезрепрее рдЗрддрд┐ рд╖рдЯреНрд╖рд╖реНрдЯрд┐рддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдореН рдПрдХрд╛рджрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее
